\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Derived$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base$<$ Derived $>$}
Base class for all 1D and 2D array, and related expressions. 

An array is similar to a dense vector or matrix. While matrices are mathematical objects with well defined linear algebra operators, an array is just a collection of scalar values arranged in a one or two dimensionnal fashion. As the main consequence, all operations applied to an array are performed coefficient wise. Furthermore, arrays support scalar math functions of the c++ standard library (e.\+g., std\+::sin(x)), and convenient constructors allowing to easily write generic code working for both scalar values and arrays.

This class is the base that is inherited by all array expression types.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Derived} & is the derived type, e.\+g., an array or an expression type.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
This class can be extended with the help of the plugin mechanism described on the page Topic\+Customizing\+\_\+\+Plugins by defining the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+ARRAYBASE\+\_\+\+PLUGIN}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}, Topic\+Class\+Hierarchy 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_aae5d1acb616f0c1f6052c3383574471c} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1numext_1_1equal__to}{numext\+::equal\+\_\+to}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_afb7b2685ceefcc46399a2a3ea4c34c67}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const Other\+Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2ArrayBase_8h_a140b988ffa480af0799d873ce22898f2}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}

template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1numext_1_1not__equal__to}{numext\+::not\+\_\+equal\+\_\+to}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_afb7b2685ceefcc46399a2a3ea4c34c67}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const Other\+Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Not\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2ArrayBase_8h_a140b988ffa480af0799d873ce22898f2}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise != operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}

This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of erf(\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{expm1()}{expm1()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a2653aab701b99d90f161f36e6581bbe7} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a0d4e7673ae36eb344fb5a183788e40ce}{Expm1\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::expm1 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise exponential of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this minus 1.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In exact arithmetic, {\ttfamily x.\+expm1()} is equivalent to {\ttfamily x.\+exp()} -\/ 1, however, with finite precision, this function is much more accurate when {\ttfamily x} is close to zero.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{log1p()}{log1p()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a438640146f3e7488f09a4f60c305b1d9} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_af4bd7e9f69ceed8d00e71f11456de311}{Log1p\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::log1p (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise logarithm of 1 plus {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In exact arithmetic, {\ttfamily x.\+log()} is equivalent to {\ttfamily }(x+1).\doxylink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2synchronization_2mutex_8cc_ae81d3246bfc238875eaecb9aff755a2e}{log()}, however, with finite precision, this function is much more accurate when {\ttfamily x} is close to zero.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ac2bbbcf6db4b01cea5caeb5aadb4b1d8}\index{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}!ndtri@{ndtri}}
\index{ndtri@{ndtri}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ndtri()}{ndtri()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ac2bbbcf6db4b01cea5caeb5aadb4b1d8} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_af4f094facf6fce6efedbb6582d187138}{Ndtri\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::ndtri (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise inverse of the CDF of the Normal distribution function function of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

In other words, considering {\ttfamily x = ndtri(y)}, it returns the argument, x, for which the area under the Gaussian probability density function (integrated from minus infinity to x) is equal to y.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of ndtri(\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\href{group__CoeffwiseMathFunctions.html\#cwisetable_ndtri}{\texttt{ Math functions}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} Derived \& \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase}{Eigen\+::\+Dense\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::operator= (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Copies the generic expression {\itshape other} into \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this. 

The expression must provide a (templated) eval\+To(\+Derived\& dst) const function which does the actual job. In practice, this allows any user to write its own special matrix without having to modify \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}

a reference to \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise != operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise square root of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes the coefficient-\/wise square root. The function Matrix\+Base\+::sqrt() in the unsupported module Matrix\+Functions computes the matrix square root.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ad996aade2210f810f1b11d43a611b1e3} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename DerivedQ $>$ \\
const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__zeta__op}{internal\+::scalar\+\_\+zeta\+\_\+op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_afb7b2685ceefcc46399a2a3ea4c34c67}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const DerivedQ $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::zeta (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2ArrayBase_8h_a140b988ffa480af0799d873ce22898f2}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS}}$<$ DerivedQ $>$ \&}]{q}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise zeta function.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

It returns the Riemann zeta function of two arguments {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape q\+:} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em q} & is the shift, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this is the exponent, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 1. 

This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of zeta(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
This method is an alias for zeta(\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this,q);
